Acrobatics | Description | Acrobatics is a keystone passive skill that causes spell suppression modifiers to grant spell dodge chance instead, at half their value. Spell dodge prevents spell hits , and is capped at 75%.
Acrobatics | Mechanics | The chance to dodge rolls independently per spell hit; it is not entropy-based like evasion. Spell dodge occurs before block and other damage mitigation.
Acrobatics | Location | Acrobatics lies on the far right side of the skill tree across the Ranger's starting area.

All Hands | Description | All Hands was an Atlas passive skill and Atlas keystone.
All Hands | Mechanics | All Hands adds a 40% chance to encounter a random master when a master mission is not selected on the map device , increasing it to 50% chance to encounter a random master. This 50% value is split evenly between the four masters by default using a weighting system of 1:1:1:1 for Einhar/Niko/Alva/Jun respectively, and can be modified by the notables that affect randomly encountered Masters in your Maps have #% increased chance to be a specific Master ( Hunting Season , Mining Partnership , Archaeology Tour , and Covert Stakeouts ), skewing a 12.5% chance to encounter a specific master to 20%.
All Hands | Mechanics | It also disables the ability to gain a master mission on completing a map. Note that while this disables the gaining of Kirac missions, it does not enable Kirac to be encountered in a map.
All Hands | Mechanics | Modifiers to chance to grant an additional Master Mission on Map Completion instead apply to chance for that Master to be randomly encountered in your Maps at 150% of their value causes passives that read Your Maps have #% chance to grant an additional (Einhar/Niko/Alva/Jun) Mission on Completion to apply a flat chance instead to encounter that master. This means that 10% to gain a specific master's mission is translated into 15% chance for that specific master to be randomly encountered , stacking additively with the 50% above. Each master can gain up to 10% mission chance on the tree (12% with Wandering Path ), or 15% (18%) chance to encounter a master in a map. By investing into multiple masters to get a total of ≥34% mission chance across the four masters, it is possible to encounter random masters in every map.
All Hands | Mechanics | Examples (with Jun as the desired master):

All That Glitters | Mechanics | Allocating this node provides a 10% chance for each shrine in your maps to instead be a Covetous Shrine.

Ancestral Bond | Description | Ancestral Bond is a keystone passive skill that raises the active totem limit by one. As a drawback, the character cannot deal damage directly.
Ancestral Bond | Mechanics | With Ancestral Bond, damage may only be dealt through indirect means such as proxies , minions , and sources unaffected by offensive damage modifiers like reflect , Master Toxicist , or Flame Surge 's burning ground. Despite specifying 'with skills ', this effect is not limited to skills, and will prevent damage by the character's non-skill explosions. [1] It does not prevent self-damage.
Ancestral Bond | Mechanics | While Ancestral Bond prevents damage and effects that require damage, it does not prevent hits or critical strikes. Effects like Culling Strike Support or Power Charge On Critical Support may be used normally.
Ancestral Bond | Location | Ancestral Bond lies on the outer northwest side of the tree, between Templar and Witch, near the Primal Manifestation totem cluster.

Arbitrary Tenets | Description | Arbitrary Tenets is an Atlas passive skill and Atlas keystone , specifically for the Ritual league encounter.
Arbitrary Tenets | Mechanics | Arbitrary Tenets causes Favours at Ritual Altars in your maps to randomly cost between 90% less and 80% more. These cost alterations are retained on deferred Rewards.
Arbitrary Tenets | Mechanics | As an example, something which costed 1000 Tribute before now has a range of 100 to 1800 Tribute with this Atlas keystone allocated. This averages out to 95% (950 in this case) of the Tribute costs, technically a net benefit overall as long as the player has sufficient tribute to account for the higher variability.
Arbitrary Tenets | Location | As of version 3.22.0, it is located near the center-left of the Atlas passive skill tree inside the Ritual cluster containing Profitable Prayers and Flexible Dogma.

Armour Mastery (passive skill) | Description | Armour Mastery was a notable passive skill.
Arrow Dancing | Description | Arrow Dancing (formerly known as Arrow Dodging and later Ondar's Guile ) is a keystone passive skill that increases the chance to evade projectile attacks , while decreasing the chance to evade melee attacks.
Arrow Dancing | Specifics | Projectile attacks include almost all arrows, spines, or spikes that are launched. Arrow Dancing has no effect on spell projectiles, as spells cannot be evaded. Community resources such as poedb.tw can be helpful in determining which monster attacks are classified as projectile or melee.
Arrow Dancing | Location | Arrow Dancing is located at the southeast edge of the tree.
Arsenal of Vengeance | Description | Arsenal of Vengeance is a keystone passive skill that causes Retaliation skills to become usable after every sixth hit you take from enemies, instead of their original conditions.
Arsenal of Vengeance | Mechanics | This keystone circumvents the need to block to enable the use of most Retaliation skills, which may be useful for builds with little to no block chance (i.e. non-staff 2-handed builds) or if you lose block chance via the map modifier of Vulnerability - Players cannot Block , Players cannot Suppress Spell Damage , 5% increased Pack size, 8% increased Rarity of Items found in this Area , 13% increased Quantity of Items found in this Area , 50% more Scarabs found in Area (Suffix). However, it can potentially cause longer delays in availability of the skill if the player can block normally; at 17% block chance or higher, you will on average be able to activate Retaliation skills more frequently than with Arsenal of Vengeance.
Arsenal of Vengeance | Mechanics | Note that Arsenal of Vengeance does NOT enable the use of Vengeful Cry , as the keystone only allows "Damaging Retaliation Skills" to become usable. Even with Corrupting Cry Support , Vengeful Cry is not considered a damaging retaliation skill.
Arsenal of Vengeance | Location | Arsenal of Vengeance lies on the far bottom left side of the skill tree between the Marauder's and Duelist's starting areas.
Arsenal of Vengeance | Related unique items | These unique items have the Arsenal of Vengeance modifier, which provides the same effect as this keystone. Taking the keystone in addition to equipping one of these items will impart no additional benefit.

Art of the Gladiator | Description | It also removes inherent movement speed penalties from body armours and shields , effectively granting up to 11% increased movement speed depending on what the character has equipped. Only the "hidden" movement speed penalties from body armours and shields are affected, so additional reduced movement speed modifiers from unique items such as Greed's Embrace will still apply.
Art of the Gladiator | Location | Art of the Gladiator is in the Duelist area, just after the Attack Speed small passives leading out of the Duelist's starting location. It connects to the Bravery - Mana Flows , Dervish , and Fury Bolts passive skill clusters.
Art of the Gladiator | Location | this info is verified in version 3.21, but the current version of the game may differ.

Avatar of Fire | Description | Avatar of Fire is a keystone passive skill that converts 50% of physical damage , lightning damage and cold damage to fire damage. However, the character cannot deal damage with any damage types except fire.
Avatar of Fire | Description | Like other offensive stats, Avatar of Fire's conversion and Deal no Non-Fire Damage do not affect self-damage such as Blood Rage or Forbidden Rite.
Avatar of Fire | Description | In most situations, Avatar of Fire will not synergize with Elemental Equilibrium , since Elemental Equilibrium will add fire resistance to the enemy, while the player is unable to utilize the cold and lightning weakness. One notable use case is when the player summons minions that primarily deal cold and lightning damage. Since minions do not inherit Elemental Equilibrium, the player's fire damage will permanently weaken the enemy to cold and lightning.
Avatar of Fire | Location | Avatar of Fire is located on the left side of the skill tree between the Templar and Marauder starting areas.
Avatar of Fire | Related unique items | These unique items have the Avatar of Fire modifier, which provides the same effect as this keystone. Taking the keystone in addition to equipping one of these items will impart no additional benefit.

Warlock of the Mists that grants the Ravenous skill | Blood Hunt | Description | Blood Hunt is a notable Ascendancy passive skill for the Warlock of the Mists that grants the Ravenous skill. Allocating this passive also grants the ability to see a monster 's monster category under their health bar.
Blood Magic | Description | Blood Magic (often referred to as BM ) is a keystone passive skill that converts all mana cost and reservation to use life instead. It also gives you more maximum life and removes your mana.
Blood Magic | Mechanics | Skills that reserve mana will reserve life and skills that cost mana will cost life instead. Mods that affect mana cost and mana reservation such as X% increased/reduced Mana Cost of Skills , + X to Total Mana Cost of Skills and X% increased/reduced Mana Reservation Efficiency of Skills have no effect on the life cost and life reservation of skills. It is not possible to commit suicide through Blood Magic.
Blood Magic | Mechanics | If taken with Eldritch Battery , your energy shield will continue to protect mana but will not be spent.
Blood Magic | Mechanics | While you have Blood Magic, you are neither at full mana nor low mana. [1]
Blood Magic | Mechanics | Taking this keystone along with Sanguimancy from Warlock of the Mists will provide the 50% increased Life Reservation Efficiency of Skills stat, but otherwise impart no additional benefit.
Blood Magic | Location | Blood Magic is located in the bottom left corner of the tree.
Blood Magic | Related unique items | These unique items have the Blood Magic modifier, which provides the same effect as this keystone. Taking the keystone in addition to equipping one of these items will impart no additional benefit.

Chainbreaker | Description | Chainbreaker is a Timeless Jewel -only keystone passive skill. It grants rage regeneration based on mana regeneration , prevents mana recovery from regeneration, and adds a base cost of 3 rage to skills. Rage gained from this keystone does not delay inherent rage loss.
Chainbreaker | Mechanics | The rage cost is affected by cost modifiers, such as multipliers on support gems, but also global modifiers such as Tireless , Fanaticism , or Indigon. Note that the vast majority of skill cost modifiers are specific for mana , which do not apply to rage costs.
Chainbreaker | Mechanics | Note that this passive's rage regeneration Does not delay Inherent Loss of Rage , meaning that for rage to be gained, rage regeneration must either exceed the inherent loss per second (10 by default), or rage loss must first be delayed in another way (e.g. with Vengeance ).
Chainbreaker | Location | This keystone will conquer any keystones within the jewel radius of a Lethal Pride that has modifier Commanded leadership over (10000–18000) warriors under Akoya.

Chaos Inoculation | Description | Chaos Inoculation (often referred to as CI ) is a keystone passive skill that grants immunity to chaos damage , but sets maximum life to 1.
Chaos Inoculation | Description | Although the character must survive entirely on energy shield instead of life, immunity to chaos damage can be a significant advantage.
Chaos Inoculation | Interactions | The chance and duration of both being stunned and receiving an elemental status ailments is based on your maximum life before CI takes effect [1]. Maximum Life modifiers such as increased maximum Life , reduced maximum Life , etc. apply to the life before CI is applied. Since this base life value is then overwritten by CI, the only advantage life modifiers provide to a CI character is the reduction on stun and status ailment thresholds.
Chaos Inoculation | Interactions | Low life conditions will never take effect while CI is enabled. Effects such as Pain Attunement and On Low Life mods on gear will not activate. For these effects, you must have 50% or less of your current maximum life. Chaos Inoculation sets your maximum life to 1. The exception to this is if you have Coward's Legacy equipped.
Chaos Inoculation | Interactions | Full life conditions will always take effect because you are always at 100% of 1 life, making the condition of Damage on Full Life Support easy to maintain.
Chaos Inoculation | Interaction with life reduction | Life reductions apply before CI which sets life to 1. For example from Ephemeral Edge. Obtaining 100%+ reduced Maximum Life will not affect the 1 Life value.
Chaos Inoculation | Blood Magic | When linked with Lifetap Support or Arrogance Support , or while taking the Blood Magic Keystone or other similar effects, affected skills (including auras) cannot be cast, unless the skill has 0 Cost and/or Reservation. The mod Skills Cost no Mana or Life while Focussed thus allows CI builds to cast skills with Life Costs (e.g. Reap , Corrupting Fever or Blood Rage ).
Chaos Inoculation | Chaos resistance reduction/penetration | Since CI grants a flat-out immunity to chaos damage, effects that reduce or penetrate chaos resistance (i.e. Occultist 's Void Beacon ) have no effect against CI. [2]
Chaos Inoculation | Being Poisoned | Being Immune to Chaos Damage means that Chaos Damage cannot inflict poison (to the entity immune to chaos damage), although physical damage can still inflict poison.
Chaos Inoculation | CI builds | It is generally best to wait until you have high energy shield before taking CI because it's much easier to survive on life at lower levels. Don't be afraid to take life passive skills for survivability while leveling up, since you can remove them later.
Chaos Inoculation | CI builds | Characters with CI are usually more susceptible to stun and status ailments because of their low base life. Rather than taking otherwise useless life nodes as described above, Stun can be mitigated by obtaining Stun Immunity (e.g Vile Bastion ), stacking Chance to Avoid Stuns, or through niche items such as Skyforth or Valyrium. Status ailments can be mitigated or avoided in a variety of different ways, including Pantheon Powers , Purity of Elements , Chance to Avoid Ailments, Reduced Effect/Duration of Ailments on You, or niche items such as Auxium.
Chaos Inoculation | CI builds | Chaos Inoculation works well with some other keystone passives, such as:
Chaos Inoculation | Location | Chaos Inoculation is located on the northeast edge of the skill tree.

Cleansed Thoughts | Description | Cleansed Thoughts is a notable passive skill that doubles chaos resistance , including both positive and negative modifiers to it. [1]
Cleansed Thoughts | Description | You can only acquire this passive through Anointment (using Oils ) on an Amulet or valid Blight Unique item.
Cleansed Thoughts | Mechanics | With this passive an endgame character who normally has a -60% base chaos resistance (due to the resistance penalties from fighting Kitava ) will have a base of -120% chaos resistance.
Cleansed Thoughts | Mechanics | However the value of positive modifiers to Chaos resistance will also be doubled, which means you will need around 28% less (98% needed vs 135% normally) chaos resistance than normal to reach the cap of 75% from there.
Cleansed Thoughts | Mechanics | The value of this passive also increases slightly the higher your chaos resistance cap is, with you needing around 30% less resistance to reach the final maximum resistance cap of 90% (105% needed vs 150% normally.)
Cleansed Thoughts | Mechanics | While this passive can allow you to reach your chaos resistance cap more easily, note that if you have any source of negative chaos resistance (due to things like curses and other items such as Oskarm ,) having Cleansed Thoughts would also double these penalties, potentially cancelling out any benefit.
Cleansed Thoughts | Anointment | Blight anointment to unlock the passive:

Deadly Inclinations | Anointment | Blight anointment to unlock the passive:
Deadly Nightmare | Description | Deadly Nightmare was an atlas passive skill.
Deadly Prey | Description | Deadly Prey is an atlas passive skill associated with Bestiary.
Deadly Prey | Mechanics | When Einhar attempts to capture a red or yellow beast, the beast has a 50% chance to break free of Einhar's trap, restore to full health, and gain a stack of Bestial Rage. Beasts can break free multiple times. Each stack of Bestial Rage grants the monster increased damage, increased attack speed, and increased character size. Defeating beasts with Bestial Rage grants the player stacks of the Hunters' Cunning buff. Hunters' Cunning persists through area changes in maps such as entering boss rooms or entering the Sacred Grove.
Deadly Prey | Mechanics | Each stack of this buff grants 2% less Damage taken from Beasts , 10% increased Damage to Beasts , 5% increased Item Quantity from slain Beasts , and 5% increased Item Rarity from slain Beasts. The less damage taken stat is capped and does not grant damage immunity at 50+ stacks. Additionally, after a player gains Hunters' Cunning , monsters with the beast monster category will have the beast icon displayed below their life bar, similar to equipping Veruso's Ambition.
Deadly Prey | Mechanics | Note that the Hunter's Cunning buff's stats apply to all monsters with the beast /animal tag, not just Bestiary monsters. [1]
Deadly Prey | Location | It is located on the Bestiary cluster near the middle of the left side of the tree.

Death Offering | Description | Death Offering is a notable Bloodline Ascendancy passive skill from the Catarina Bloodline that grants increased Offering effect, but causes all damageable entities that are affected by the Offering buffs to be killed when the Offering expires.
Death Offering | Mechanics | Death will not occur if the offering is replaced before the offering's duration fully expires, or if the offering buff is removed prematurely (e.g. unsocketing the gem or weapon swapping). It does not have to be replaced by the same offering skill. However, if you can have multiple offerings (e.g. Leash of Oblation ), only using the same offering skill can replace an offering's duration, and the first offering to expire will cause death even if other offerings have remaining duration.
Death Offering | Mechanics | This passive can kill the player character if the player can be affected their own Offering skills (e.g. Mistress of Sacrifice , The Queen's Hunger ). In hideouts , this effect is non-fatal and will leave the character at 1 life.
Death Offering | Mechanics | This passive can also kill the character if they are linked to a minion that dies from this passive. In hideouts, only the minion will die; the character will not suffer death or life loss from this passive from a linked minion.

Decay Ward | Anointment | Blight anointment to unlock the passive:

Destructive Play | Description | Destructive Play is an Atlas keystone passive skill that causes the Maven to use the "Up the Stakes" skill when witnessing map bosses , summoning 1 to 3 additional bosses. The number of additional bosses summoned by Up the Stakes is higher if there are fewer monsters remaining in the map.
Destructive Play | Mechanics | Destructive Play causes the Maven to always use the skill "Up the Stakes", which summons 1-3 additional random bosses when witnessing a map boss in a map, depending on the number of monsters remaining on the map. Fewer remaining monsters will make it more likely to spawn 3 additional random bosses. Maven can summon additional bosses even if the map boss is killed before she casts the skill. These additional bosses do not count towards having been witnessed by the Maven, but drop items as if they were witnessed Final Map Bosses. Modifiers to Final Map Bosses apply to these summoned bosses which include the following:
Destructive Play | Mechanics | Despite not specifying final map bosses, Conquered Conquerors also provides similar effects as Remnants of the Past and Vivid Memories as map bosses have a base chance to drop Elderslayer maps in general.
Destructive Play | Mechanics | Domination Scarab of Terrors and Horned Scarab of Pandemonium can also be used to add additional "Final" Map Bosses to the map to benefit from the above passives or items.
Destructive Play | Mechanics | In a Conqueror map, if the Maven is unable to cast the skill on the default map boss, she will instead cast it inside the Conqueror's arena.
Destructive Play | Mechanics | In an Elder Guardian map, Maven uses the skill only in the Elder Guardian's third/final phase.
Destructive Play | Mechanics | Caution is advised as the Maven can randomly summon bosses with a corpse explosion skill (e.g. Detonate Dead ) such as Maligaro the Mutilator , Tolman, the Exhumer , Kalria, The Risen , Witch of the Cauldron , or Enticer of Rot.
Destructive Play | Strategies | While running the same map multiple times is typically not possible with Maven-witnessed maps (as the Maven will not witness an already witnessed map), it is possible to strategically use certain phased map bosses to prevent accidentally killing the map's default boss, but spawn the additional map bosses from Up the Stakes to be farmed for Final Map Boss rewards before exiting. Note that with this strategy, as the player does not kill the map's boss, the map will not be counted as completed and can continue to be witnessed. Some examples include:
Destructive Play | Strategies | Other bosses may have immunity phases, but can still be killed before they activate, or may be too short to reliably avoid accidentally killing the boss.
Destructive Play | Ruthless mode | In Ruthless mode , the Maven only has a 20% chance to summon additional random bosses.
Destructive Play | Location | As of version 3.22.0 it is located near the top of the Atlas passive skill tree inside the Maven cluster.

Divine Flesh | Description | Divine Flesh is a keystone passive skill that causes you to take 50% of elemental damage as chaos damage and grants additional maximum chaos resistance, but causes all damage to bypass energy shield.
Divine Flesh | Mechanics | While this keystone has negative synergy with Chaos Inoculation , it can still be used with Eldritch Battery.
Divine Flesh | Mechanics | For more information about taking damage as another element, see Damage taken as.
Divine Flesh | Mechanics | The damage taken over time effect of Righteous Fire and other non-chaos degenerations will also be converted. As such, Divine Flesh can be an excellent way to reduce the degeneration effect, granted that a player has capped their chaos resistance.
Divine Flesh | Mechanics | Divine Flesh will take precedence over modifiers that prevent damage from bypassing energy shield, such as those found on Shavronne's Wrappings , Solaris Lorica or Emperor's Vigilance. This means that all damage will continue to bypass energy shield, making those items negative synergies. [1]
Divine Flesh | Location | This keystone can only be obtained by placing a Glorious Vanity unique Timeless Jewel (only variants that have the modifier Bathed in the blood of (100-8000) sacrificed in the name of Xibaqua ) into a socket on the skill tree, or other unique item that grant this keystone. It is not on the default passive tree.
Divine Flesh | Location | Any keystone within the radius of the jewel's area of effect will be converted (in-game wording: conquered ) into Divine Flesh, allowing the player to allocate it.

Elemental Equilibrium | Description | Elemental Equilibrium (often referred to as EE ) is a keystone passive skill. Whenever you deal any elemental damage with a hit , it applies fire , cold , or lightning exposure of the element(s) that the hit didn't deal the element of, and removes the exposure type of the element(s) that did.
Elemental Equilibrium | Mechanics | Only a hit that deals damage will apply the respective exposure. Blocked hits or damage over time will not trigger Elemental Equilibrium.
Elemental Equilibrium | Mechanics | If you hit an enemy with two different elements at the same time it will apply exposure to the third element and remove the other two element exposure. A hit carrying all three elements types will not apply exposure and will remove all of them. [1]
Elemental Equilibrium | Mechanics | Trap , Mine , and Totem skills trigger EE as they use your skills with your offensive stats, which includes keystones and passives. Minions do not trigger EE as they do not use your skills or stats, and are only affected by keystones and passives that explicitly mention minions. [2] One way to trigger EE via minions is socketing the minion gem into a Malachai's Artifice.
Elemental Equilibrium | Mechanics | Multiple attacks that hit simultaneously are still processed independently, so the first hit that is processed will trigger EE that affects the other hits. [3]
Elemental Equilibrium | Mechanics | Elemental Equilibrium as a whole applies before regular on-hit exposure. A hit that deals fire damage and therefore removes fire exposure can still inflict fire exposure with e.g. Eye of Malice or an eldritch glove implicit.
Elemental Equilibrium | Example uses | As long as you are careful to not use the same element twice in a row, EE can greatly boost damage. Try to use a combination of skills that alternate between two elements, or cycles through all three:
Elemental Equilibrium | Location | Elemental Equilibrium is located on the bottom right side of the tree, on the intersection between the Scion, Duelist, and Ranger paths.

Elemental Equilibrium | Unique items | The following unique items are related to Elemental Equilibrium:

Elemental Overload | Description | Elemental Overload (often referred to as EO ) is a keystone passive skill that causes skills to deal 40% more elemental damage with hits and ailments for 8 seconds after that skill deals a critical strike , but prevents any interactions between critical strikes and ailments. When the damage multiplier is active for a skill, it is indicated by a diamond on the bottom of that skill's icon in the skill bar.
Elemental Overload | Mechanics | Skills that have dealt a Critical Strike in the past 8 seconds deal 40% more Elemental Damage with Hits and Ailments : When a skill deals a critical strike , it gains more elemental damage for 8 seconds, limited to hits and ailments.
Elemental Overload | Mechanics | Skills used by proxies such as totems , traps , or mines will activate Elemental Overload for the player's skill when they crit, which will then apply to all uses of that skill, including by those proxies. Minions are unaffected by Elemental Overload, even the skill that summoned them can crit (e.g. Absolution ).
Elemental Overload | Mechanics | Per conversion mechanics, Elemental Overload's 40% more Elemental Damage will apply to physical damage converted into elemental, and elemental damage converted into chaos. Additionally, because inflicting damaging ailments with base damage of a different type is treated similar to conversion , Elemental Overload will apply to poison originating from damage that was elemental at any point. [2] For example, poison inflicted with lightning damage damage through Volkuur's Guidance 's Your Lightning Damage can Poison.
Elemental Overload | Mechanics | Ailments never count as being from Critical Strikes : This stat prevents your ailments from ever being counted as from a critical strike, even if the hit applying the ailment did critically strike. Consequentially, any Damage over Time Multiplier for Ailments from Critical Strikes and similar conditional modifiers no longer apply. This includes the character's inherent +50% DoT multiplier on crit, passives like Dire Torment , and gems like Critical Strike Affliction Support.
Elemental Overload | Strategy | Elemental Overload is best allocated on characters that do not invest in critical strike but still deal critical strikes occasionally. Modifiers to critical strike multiplier no longer have any effect and can be ignored when assessing equipment.
Elemental Overload | Strategy | Ideally, when Elemental Overload is allocated, the player will strive to deal at least one critical strike every 8 seconds in order to keep the damage effect active. This can be achieved by balancing critical strike chance and hit rate. An average of one critical strike every 8 seconds is achieved by performing 12.5/(Critical Strike Chance) hits per second. For example, with the minimum critical strike chance of 5%, a character who performs 2.5 hits per second will on average deal a critical strike every 8 seconds (this assumes your accuracy for melee/ranged weapons allows a 100% chance to hit).
Elemental Overload | Elemental Overload and Ignite | Although the 40% More Elemental Damage modifier may seem less powerful than the +50% to damage over time multiplier an Ignite applied by a Critical Strike would apply, note that damage over time multipliers are additive with each other. EO's 40% More modifier, on the other hand, is multiplicative with all other modifiers. If you have at least +25% to your current DoT multiplier, EO will grant your Ignites more damage than the additional DoT multiplier with a crit. EO also only requires that you crit occasionally, rather than with each Ignite.
Elemental Overload | Elemental Overload vs Critical Strikes? | This table compares average damage of critical strikes versus elemental overload (with green indicating Elemental Overload is better than Critical Strikes).
Elemental Overload | Elemental Overload vs Critical Strikes? | It assumes that you have a 100% uptime on elemental overload.
Elemental Overload | Elemental Overload vs Critical Strikes? | The crit chance used in the table is effective crit chance, i.e. the real critical strike chance including accuracy.
Elemental Overload | Location | Elemental Overload is located at the middle layer of the northwest part of the tree, near the transition area between Witch and Templar.

Endless Tide | Description | Endless Tide is an Atlas passive skill and Atlas keystone , specifically for the Beyond league encounter.
Endless Tide | Mechanics | Endless Tide prevents Beyond bosses from spawning, but also halves the total Beyond portal merging radius. While this prevents the Beyond mechanic from ending prematurely by spawning a boss, it also reduces the number of additional Beyond monsters that you would otherwise spawn from portal merging. However, this downside can be negated with extremely dense maps, in which the portal merging reduction would not have a significant impact, and would be where Beyond shines with this keystone.
Endless Tide | Location | As of version 3.22.0 it is located near the center-left of the Atlas passive skill tree connected to the Beyond cluster containing Scent of Blood.

Eternal Youth | Description | Eternal Youth is a keystone passive skill which causes energy shield recharge to apply to life , but halves your life regeneration and life leech.
Eternal Youth | Mechanics | Your life recharge rate is dependent on your total life pool, not your energy shield pool.
Eternal Youth | Mechanics | As with energy shield, taking damage to life will interrupt the recharge. Taking damage to energy shield or mana will not interrupt life recharge.
Eternal Youth | Mechanics | Modifiers that prevent energy shield recharge, such as Ghost Reaver and Shavronne's Revelation , do not prevent life recharge.
Eternal Youth | Mechanics | Modifiers to energy shield recharge, such as faster start of energy shield recharge and increased energy shield recharge rate , apply to life recharge instead. Wicked Ward prevents life recharge from being interrupted.
Eternal Youth | Mechanics | The less Life Regeneration Rate mod on the keystone does not lower energy shield regeneration when Zealot's Oath keystone is allocated.
Eternal Youth | Location | Eternal Youth is located on the west side of the tree, on the intersection between the Scion, Marauder, and Templar paths.
Eternal Youth | Location | This keystone can also be obtained from the tree by using a legacy Glorious Vanity jewel with modifier Bathed in the blood of (100–8000) sacrificed in the name of Zerphi. The jewel will conquer any keystones within the radius (size: 1500) of the jewel.

Everlasting Sacrifice | Description | Everlasting Sacrifice is a keystone passive skill that grants a temporary buff to maximum resistances when the character reaches full energy shield , then sacrifices all energy shield.
Everlasting Sacrifice | Sources | Everlasting Sacrifice can be obtained from the following sources:
Everlasting Sacrifice | Mechanics | Everlasting Sacrifice will activate whenever you recover energy shield past your maximum. ES gained from recharge will also count. You do not need to be at less than full energy shield to proc Everlasting Sacrifice. Everlasting Sacrifice will not function if you have 0 maximum energy shield.
Everlasting Sacrifice | Mechanics | Everlasting Sacrifice is unaffected by modifiers to buff effect or duration.
Everlasting Sacrifice | Strategy | To maintain full uptime of +5% to all Maximum Resistances, the player's energy shield must be able to reach full energy shield at least once every 4 seconds. This is best achieved by reducing your maximum ES as low as possible while stacking ES recovery, preferably flat regen and ES gain on hit. Percentage ES recovery that scales with maximum ES, including recharge and ES leech, are less viable due to it being much slower.
Everlasting Sacrifice | Strategy | Some choices of viable energy shield recovery include:
Everlasting Sacrifice | Strategy | Reducing the energy shield pool is generally preferred, which provides some use to items like Daresso's Salute , Ming's Heart , or reflected jewelry with negative maximum energy shield mods, or by minimizing increases to ES by redirecting Intelligence bonuses with Solipsism , Faithguard , or Crystallised Omniscience. The only exception would be for Energy Blade builds, which instead want to maximize ES and use % sources of ES recovery instead (stacking Strength and Intelligence, using Shaper's Touch , etc). Note that you would need to cast Energy Blade prior to equipping the shield, as the skill costs Energy Shield to use.
Everlasting Sacrifice | Strategy | Note that maintaining Everlasting Sacrifice will be significantly harder if the sources of Everlasting Sacrifice also adds additional maximum ES (e.g. Mahuxotl's Machination and Foulborn Soul Tether without both Foulborn mods). Otherwise, you will need only a miniscule amount of maximum ES above 0 to maintain it.
Everlasting Sacrifice | Strategy | With Eldritch Battery , you can maintain permanent uptime by scaling recharge rate. You will need at least 50% increased recharge rate plus extra to maintain your skill costs to maintain permanent uptime with recharge rate alone.
Everlasting Sacrifice | Unique items | Droppable unique item related to Everlasting Sacrifice:

Explosive Force | Description | Explosive Force is a notable passive skill only found on a Large Cluster Jewel that have an enchantment Added Small Passive Skills grant: Wand Attacks deal 12% increased Damage with Hits and Ailments , or a Megalomaniac.
Explosive Force | Mechanics | Unlike most explosions , this notable's explosion is considered an on- hit ( killing blow ) effect, causing it to be inherited by the player's skills. This means explosions may also be caused by killing blows with wand attacks from proxies , such as mines. Explosions caused this way are unaffected by the player's stats, however, as those stats are only part of the proxy's skill, not global.

Extreme Archaeology | Mechanics | Extreme Archaeology significantly increases the explosive radius and placement range for Expedition bombs in maps, but limits your number of explosives to 1. This creates a single large explosion that makes all remnants in the area apply to all enemies in the area, saving time planning and placing the explosives, and allowing you to reap more benefits from remnants than you otherwise would have.

Ghost Dance | Description | Ghost Dance is a keystone on the passive tree. It generates a Ghost Shroud every two seconds, up to a maximum of three Ghost Shrouds. When hit , a Ghost Shroud is removed and recovers energy shield equal to a percentage of your evasion rating.
Ghost Dance | Mechanics | The character must be hit in order for a Ghost Shroud to recover energy shield. Defensive mechanics that prevent hits such as evasion and dodge will also prevent the loss of Ghost Shrouds.
Ghost Dance | Mechanics | Self-hits will cause a Ghost Shroud to be lost normally. Reflected hits and blocked hits will not. Taking damage from blocked hits (e.g. through Module Error: Too many passives found with q_where = passive_skills.name="Glancing Blows" ) does not change this.
Ghost Dance | Location | Ghost Dance is located on the top-right side of the tree, on the upper outer parts of the Shadow's starting area.
Ghost Reaver | Description | Ghost Reaver is a keystone passive skill that causes the player to leech energy shield instead of life , and doubles the maximum total recovery per second from energy shield leech, with the downside of disabling energy shield recharge.
Ghost Reaver | Mechanics | Ghost Reaver makes any effect that would grant life leech grant ES leech instead, including non-standard sources of life leech, such as Machina Mitts or The Baron. This is not a conversion mechanic; life leech modifiers will not apply to leech altered by this keystone. Only modifiers to ES leech apply. [1]
Ghost Reaver | Mechanics | Maximum total Energy Shield Recovery per second refers to the cap on per-second recovery from all existing leech instances, and is normally 10% of maximum ES. Doubling it happens after increases or reductions.
Ghost Reaver | Location | Ghost Reaver is located on the top-right side of the tree, away from the Shadow's starting area.

Grand Design | Unique items | The following unique items are related to Grand Design:
Grand Design (Atlas keystone) | Description | Grand Design was an atlas passive skill and Atlas keystone.
Grand Design (Atlas keystone) | Mechanics | Disables the effects of all small passive skills, but adds 1% pack size per notable allocated. The most popular use of this keystone is to farm extremely dense Breaches , Legions , Abysses , Expeditions , and Exarch/Eater packs for experience and Logbooks. It also benefits Delirium , Ritual , Harbinger , shrines , and Beyond. Depending on the player's atlas tree, it is fairly easy to achieve double or more the default pack size of monsters in maps. The passives which block off league mechanics are most efficient with this. Using Sextant modifiers which force a league mechanic to appear with it are recommended, as their appearance rates are significantly lowered without small passives.
Grand Design (Atlas keystone) | Ruthless mode | In Ruthless mode , instead of granting increased pack size per notable, it grants 20 Atlas passive skill points.

Grasp the Past | Mechanics | The rolled number of memory strands on equipment found in maps has a chance to be lucky.

Useful for getting rid of less valuable scarabs without converting them into other random scarabs at lesser returns, and for juicing content that likes to have large pack sizes like Delirium. The bonus to pack size is applied after any map modifiers and increased effect of them.

Huntleader | Description | Huntleader is a notable Bloodline Ascendancy passive skill from the Farrul Bloodline that triggers the skill Summon Spectral Tiger on critical strike.
Huntleader | Mechanics | Summon Spectral Tiger : Summon Spectral Tigers function nearly identically to Summon Spectral Wolf. Like Spectral Wolves, Spectral Tigers are minions that attack using melee strikes for a base 30 second duration and the owner's modifiers to claw critical strike chance and multiplier apply to the minions. Spectral Tigers also inherently have the modifier 100% of Physical Attack Damage Leeched as Life. Up to 5 can be alive at a time and summoning a Spectral Tiger while at maximum will refresh the duration of the oldest one. Each Spectral Tiger grants 25% increased Global Critical Strike Chance , 7% increased Attack Speed , and 7% increased Cast Speed to the owner, for up to 125% increased global crit chance and 35% increased attack and cast speed.
Huntleader | Mechanics | Spectral Tiger maximum life can be seen on the Character panel.

Imbalanced Guard | Mechanics | 100% chance to Defend with 200% of Armour : Similar modifiers, such as the 20% chance to Defend with 200% of Armour Armour Mastery , do not stack with Imbalanced Guard.
Imbalanced Guard | Mechanics | Maximum Damage Reduction for any Damage Type is 50% : This modifier lowers the cap on 'damage reduction' to 50%, from 90%.
Imbalanced Guard | Mechanics | This affects damage reduction granted by armour against physical damage hits, additional sources such as #% additional Physical Damage Reduction on strength body armours and shields, and damage reduction for non-physical damage gained from effects like Endurance charges , Transcendence , Doryani's Prototype , Unbreakable , The Fourth Vow , or Eternal Damnation.
Imbalanced Guard | Mechanics | The cap does not affect non-'damage reduction' mitigations such as immunity , avoidance , resistance , damage taken modifiers (e.g. Fortification ), spell suppression , or block. [1]
Imbalanced Guard | Strategy | Imbalanced Guard can cause armour to grant higher damage reduction against bigger hits, but limits armour's effectiveness against smaller hits. This may be useful for builds that stack several types of mitigation, rather than primarily stacking armour or additional damage reduction.
Imbalanced Guard | Location | Imbalanced Guard is located at the middle layer of the southwest part of the tree, to the left of the transition path between Duelist and Marauder , next to the Soul of Steel cluster.

Iron Reflexes | Description | Iron Reflexes is a keystone passive skill that converts all evasion rating into armour. It also removes the bonus to evasion rating that dexterity inherently grants.
Iron Reflexes | Mechanics | Iron Reflexes converts evasion into armour. Similar to other forms of conversion, armour converted this way 'remembers' originating from evasion, and will include evasion modifiers in its calculation, such as Grace 's #% more Evasion rating.
Iron Reflexes | Mechanics | Armour gained from evasion equipment counts as Armour from that equipment for the purpose of effects like Prospero's Protection or Unbreakable. [1]
Iron Reflexes | Conversion Formulae | The final Armour value is calculated with the following formula: [2] [3]
Iron Reflexes | Conversion Formulae | where:
Iron Reflexes | Conversion Formulae | Modifiers which grant #% increased Evasion Rating and Armour (e.g. Bravery ) or #% increased Global Defences (e.g. Skin of the Loyal ) only apply to base values one time. For example, taking Bravery would increase flat ER by 24%, which would then be converted directly into the final Armour. It does not then apply 24% increased Armour, as the flat ER was already affected by that modifier.
Iron Reflexes | Conversion Formulae | When factoring modifiers which apply to specific equipment slots such as While a Pinnacle Atlas Boss is in your Presence, (67-70)% increased Armour from Equipped Helmet and Gloves ArmourFromHelmetGlovesEldritchImplicitPinnaclePresence6 Eater of Worlds While a Pinnacle Atlas Boss is in your Presence, (67-70)% increased Armour from Equipped Helmet and Gloves , each source of flat AR/EV should be calculated separately, then summed at the end. These modifiers are additive with other increases and reductions.
Iron Reflexes | Example | 1000 Armour from Equipped Items 1000 Evasion Rating from Equipped Items +1500 Armour from Granite Flask +1500 Evasion Rating from Jade Flask +2051 Armour from Determination +2575 Evasion Rating from Grace 80% increased Armour from passive skills 40% increased Evasion Rating from passive skills 36% increased Evasion Rating and Armour from passive skills 49% more Armour from Determination 29% more Evasion Rating from Grace
Iron Reflexes | Summary | With Iron Reflexes:
Iron Reflexes | Summary | Therefore, the mods that provide the most significant benefits in conjunction with Iron Reflexes are those that increase Armour or both Evasion Rating and Armour.
Iron Reflexes | Location | Iron Reflexes is located in the Southern part of the tree near the Duelist Section. It is a stand-alone keystone.
Iron Will | Description | Iron Will is a keystone passive skill that causes the increased melee physical attack damage bonus from strength to apply to spells as well.
Iron Will | Mechanics | Iron Will causes strength to grant 1% increased spell damage per 5 points of strength, alongside the melee physical damage bonus it already grants. Note that this bonus applies to all spell damage, not just physical.
Iron Will | Mechanics | Iron Will is a keyword and will not stack with other sources of Iron Will , such as Iron Will Support and Repentance.
Iron Will | Mechanics | Effects that modify strength's effect on melee physical damage will also affect the bonus to spell damage granted by Iron Will. For example, The Iron Fortress grants Strength's Damage Bonus instead grants 3% increased Melee Physical Damage per 10 Strength ; this will also apply to the increase in spell damage granted by Iron Will. Another notable interaction is with Crown of Eyes which grants Increases and Reductions to Spell Damage also apply to Attacks at 150% of their value , this in conjunction with Iron Will means that every 10 points of strength gives 3% increased attack damage, and if used alongside The Iron Fortress this becomes 4.5% increased attack damage per 10 strength. This increased attack damage does not stack with the original 2% increased Melee Physical Damage per 10 strength, only the higher modifier is applied.
Iron Will | Location | Iron Will is located in the center of the passive skill tree, west of the Scion starting area.

When used, the user dashes backwards and leaves behind a short-lived illusion. Enemies can destroy the illusion, causing it to apply a debuff over a large area that applies less damage dealt and increased damage taken.

Meticulous Appraiser | Description | Meticulous Appraiser is an Atlas passive skill and Atlas keystone. It applies item quantity modifiers to item rarity instead, resulting in a lower item drop rate , though with a higher chance of items becoming magic , rare or unique.
Meticulous Appraiser | Mechanics | Meticulous Appraiser causes modifiers to area item quantity to instead apply to Item Rarity at 300% of their value. This applies to sources of area quantity that apply on opening the map, such as map item quality , map modifiers , fragments , and map device crafts. The keystone does not interact with quantity or rarity added to the area at a later stage, for example with Eldritch Altars encountered inside the map.
Meticulous Appraiser | Location | As of version 3.22.0, it is located near the top of the Atlas passive skill tree.

This inventory is located to the left of the inventory menu, and can be collapsed. This inventory is deprioritised unless the primary inventory is either full or cannot fit the item the player is attempting to add to their inventory.

Minion Instability | Description | Minion Instability is a keystone passive that causes minions to explode when reduced to low life , dealing 33% of their maximum life as fire secondary damage to nearby enemies.
Minion Instability | Mechanics and Interactions | The explosion is an area hit from the minion, dealing secondary damage. The base explosion radius is 2.2 metres. [1] Its base critical strike chance is 0%.
Minion Instability | Mechanics and Interactions | Minions must be reduced to Low Life to explode. Anything that causes a minion to die without ever having low life (e.g. dying in 1 hit, replacement, expiring duration) will not cause an explosion. Minions that are set to low life when spawned, like Mirror Arrow used by a low life summoner, will explode instantly.
Minion Instability | Modifiers | Minions do not have the player's global stats; player stats have to be specific for minions or allies to directly affect the explosion. [2] Stats from auras will continue to apply to nearby minions as they explode. [3]
Minion Instability | Modifiers | Because support gems affect minions globally, the explosion can be modified by support gems despite not being a skill. The support gem needs to be compatible with the minion skill, and the support gem's stats need to be compatible with the explosion's damage. For example:
Minion Instability | Modifiers | Note: Void Manipulation Support and Brutality Support will cause the explosion to deal no fire damage.
Minion Instability | Lowering minion life | It's possible to make minions reach low life in the following ways:
Minion Instability | Lowering minion life | Affliction from the Warlock of the Mists Wildwood ascendancy can be used, but you can't activate both explosion effects unless you get the minion's life down to 20% instantly.
Minion Instability | Location | Minion Instability is located in the right side of the upper part of the tree, near the energy shield wheel for the Witch.

Necromantic Aegis | Specifics | The character will no longer benefit from any modifiers on equipped shields including implicit modifiers and explicit modifiers , local defences such as armour rating, and chance to block , and will instead apply these stats to minions.
Necromantic Aegis | Specifics | The player character is still considered as holding a shield and will be affected by the hidden movement speed penalty based on the shield's basetype. The buff from Tempest Shield will still benefit the character.
Necromantic Aegis | Specifics | Passive skills that increase stats from shields (e.g. #% increased Energy Shield from Equipped Shield will have no effect. Passive skills that provide a bonus while holding a shield, such as the elemental resistances granted by Sanctuary , will still benefit the character. [1]
Necromantic Aegis | Specifics | Increased Rarity of Items found and Increased Quantity of Items found on shields only have an effect when applied to the player, and these bonuses will be rendered useless if granted to minions. [2]
Necromantic Aegis | Specifics | Gems and Abyssal Jewels socketed in equipped shields are still usable and are not inherited by minions.
Necromantic Aegis | Specifics | Most Crucible Passives work with Necromantic Aegis. Crucible Passives that allocate notable passive skills have no effect as minions do not have access to your passive tree. [3]

Perfect Agony | Mechanics | Damage over Time Multiplier for Ailment is equal to Critical Strike Multiplier : Perfect Agony will override your DoT multiplier with ailments to be equal to your critical strike multiplier. Other sources of DoT multiplier that apply to ailment DoT multiplier, including generic and conditional DoT multiplier bonuses, will be ignored [1]. On the other hand, all sources of critical strike multiplier, including generic, local , and conditional bonuses, will apply to ailment DoT multiplier. [2]
Perfect Agony | Mechanics | Critical Strikes do not deal extra damage :This stat is similar to the one found on Ungil's Harmony. Each hit will still calculate critical strike multiplier normally (including conditional stats), but this will only be used as DoT multiplier for ailments, not extra hit damage.
Perfect Agony | Mechanics | Non-Critical Strikes cannot apply Ailments : This stat also prevents the application of non-damaging ailments on non-critical strikes.
Perfect Agony | Location | Perfect Agony is located on the east side of the passive skill tree, in the outer path between the Shadow and Ranger start locations.

Point Blank | Description | Point Blank is a keystone passive skill that scales the damage of projectile attacks with respect to the distance the projectile has travelled, increasing damage initially then reducing damage after covering a long distance.
Point Blank | Mechanics | The projectile has a maximum damage increase of 30% more near the start of its travel (up to 10 units), then linearly scales down to no damage change at 35 units, then linearly scales down again to the maximum damage penalty of 30% less at 120 units. [1] [2] [3]
Point Blank | Mechanics | It is important to note that damage scaling is done with respect to the total distance the projectile has travelled, not its current distance from the point of origin. [4] If the projectile changes direction—as is the case with Spectral Throw —distance travelled continues to increase as the projectile returns to its point of origin. Projectiles that travel in multiple segments (such as Arrow Nova Support ) include the payload distance in the damage penalty. [5]
Point Blank | Skill gem and passive skill | Point Blank Support does not stack with the passive skill. A skill either has Point Blank or does not. [6]
Point Blank | Attacks only | The Point Blank effect only works with attack projectiles.This includes projectile portions of melee weapon attacks such as Lightning Strike 's and Molten Strike 's projectiles. It does not affect spells.
Point Blank | Fork, pierce and chain | A projectile which pierces, chains or forks is still considered the same projectile, and its total travel distance is used. [7]
Point Blank | At Close Range | Chin Sol 's more damage at close range is not Point Blank and thus stack multiplicatively.
Point Blank | Projectile attacks with AoE | Point blank bonuses are calculated based on the distance from where it was fired to the enemy hit. [8] [9] [10]
Point Blank | Projectile speed | Projectile speed has no impact on the distances at which Point Blank's multipliers affect damage.
Point Blank | Far Shot | Point Blank and Far Shot are multiplicative with each other and can make damage more consistent by counteracting each others' damage penalties.
Point Blank | Location | Point Blank is located in the southeast edge of the tree.

Precise Retaliation | Unique items | The following unique items are related to Precise Retaliation:
Precise Technique | Description | Precise Technique (often referred to as PT ) is a keystone passive skill that causes you to deal 40% more Attack damage if your Accuracy Rating is higher than your Maximum Life, but prevents you from dealing critical strikes.
Precise Technique | Mechanics | Damage over Time and Ailments are never considered Attack Damage.
Precise Technique | Mechanics | Never deal Critical Strikes takes precedent over sources of guaranteed Critical Strikes such as Replica Trypanon.
Precise Technique | Strategy | Precise Technique is best allocated on characters that either have very little life (e.g Chaos Inoculation builds), can get large amounts of accuracy with minor investment (e.g. Hollow Palm Technique Dexterity stacking builds), and/or have limited passives to invest into critical strike chance and multiplier. Juggernaut can also use this by taking Undeniable ascendancy passive; however, Juggernauts typically prefer to go the crit route due to preferring to use Oskarm.
Precise Technique | Strategy | Modifiers to critical strike chance and multiplier no longer have any effect and can be ignored when assessing equipment.
Precise Technique | Strategy | Life-based builds will typically need to invest somewhat into accuracy, such as getting it on Weapons, Helmets, Gloves, Shields, Rings, or Amulets. the Accuracy Mastery "Dexterity's Accuracy Bonus instead grants +3 to Accuracy Rating per Dexterity" can be useful on right-side tree builds, and incredibly strong on Hollow Palm builds.
Precise Technique | Strategy | CI builds (due to have only 1 Maximum Life) will not need to invest any further into accuracy, having already exceeded the requirement due to the baseline accuracy obtained from Dexterity on all characters.
Precise Technique | Strategy | Additional Accuracy Support can contribute to the accuracy threshold for supported skills. Stats with a hit-specific condition such as "increased Accuracy Rating against Unique Enemies" cannot.
Precise Technique | Precise Technique vs Elemental Overload vs Critical Strikes | Precise Technique provides a more consistent damage bonus, but may be harder to reach for characters built in the Strength or Intelligence areas of the tree. Non-CI builds may require some additional investment to meet the requirement Accuracy Rating. It also will not apply to Ignite or Damage over Time, but will apply to Physical or Chaos damage attacks.
Precise Technique | Precise Technique vs Elemental Overload vs Critical Strikes | Elemental Overload provides a more generic damage bonus, applying to damage over time and Ignites, but only affects Elemental Damage (Poison dealt via Elemental Damage included), and requires the character to crit within the past 8 seconds with the damaging skill. This requires at least a certain amount of attack/cast speed, hit rate, and/or crit chance. This can be difficult to achieve for skills with long wind-ups or slow speeds (e.g. Doryani's Fist , Assailum ).
Precise Technique | Precise Technique vs Elemental Overload vs Critical Strikes | Regular critical builds have a much higher ceiling of damage, not being capped only by the 40% More multiplier, but requires additional investment in gear and passives. However, it also has other perks that are not (easily) accessible on the other two playstyles, such as easy access to Elusive or Tailwind , as well as consistent Freezes.
Precise Technique | Location | Precise Technique is located in the bottom right-area of the passive tree, between the duelist and ranger starts.
Precise Technique | Base items | The following base items are related to Precise Technique: No results found

Prolonged Servitude | Description | Prolonged Servitude is a notable Bloodline Ascendancy passive skill from the Catarina Bloodline that grants the user's minions more damage while at low life and delays their death when they take lethal damage.
Prolonged Servitude | Mechanics | Minions cannot be Killed, but die 6 seconds after being reduced to 1 Life : The actual effect of this stat is that minions that reach 0 life will persist for 6 seconds before they die , essentially a grace period. This timer cannot be modified and is not affected by duration modifiers. A misty swirl will occur on the minion, and they will gain a mist-like trail. During this state, they count as having 0 life, and cannot recover life through any method. Effects that occur on death only occur after this 6 second timer expires, not when they first reach 0 life.
Prolonged Servitude | Mechanics | Although Animate Guardian normally cannot be resummoned in the same area if it dies, with Prolonged Servitude it is possible to unsocket and resocket (or weapon swap to disable) the Animate Guardian gem during the 6 second timer to be able to cast the skill again, resummoning it without any penalty.
Prolonged Servitude | Mechanics | Minions that are killed indirectly such as through being exploded or consumed (e.g. Minion Instability , Death Wish , Aukuna's Will + corpse explosion/consumption) will not have their death prolonged and will instead die instantly.
Prospector's Luck | Description | Prospector's Luck is an atlas passive skill. It increases the chance for a map to contain ore deposits and increases the relative drop rate of Kalguuran Scarabs.

Prospero's Wager | Mechanics | This keystone causes all corpses' crafting modifiers to be hidden until they are buried, at which point they are revealed.

Purposeful Harbinger | Description | Purposeful Harbinger is a notable passive skill only found on magic or rare cluster jewel , or the unique cluster jewel Megalomaniac.
Purposeful Harbinger | Description | In specific, the magic or rare jewel must have enchantments Added Small Passive Skills grant: Minions deal 10% increased Damage while you are affected by a Herald or Added Small Passive Skills grant: 10% increased Damage while affected by a Herald (both Medium Cluster Jewel exclusive), or Added Small Passive Skills grant: 6% increased Mana Reservation Efficiency of Skills ( Small Cluster Jewel exclusive). Check the spawn weight in the table below for details.
Purposeful Harbinger | Mechanics | Purposeful Harbinger increases the effect(s) of Auras on you from your aura skill(s), up to a "global" cap of 40% shared among all Purposeful Harbinger passives. Stacking multiple copies of this notable will reduce the overall number of Heralds required to hit the maximum effect, but will not affect the maximum itself. Generally, players will use no more than two or three in combination with three or two Heralds, respectively.
Purposeful Harbinger | Mechanics | Purposeful Harbinger does not increase the effect of auras that affect enemies, such as Pride , or the increased Physical Damage taken portion of Flesh and Stone. The less damage taken portion of Flesh and Stone will still be affected, however.
Purposeful Harbinger | Mods | The mod can also be found in Medium Cluster Jewel with the legacy enchantment Added Small Passive Skills grant: 3% increased effect of Non-Curse Auras from your Skills (as "old_do_not_use_affliction_aura_effect" in the spawn weight table), with a nonzero spawn weight on jewels that have item level ≥75.

Rampant Growth | Description | Rampant Growth is an atlas passive skill.
Rampant Growth | Mechanics | Eldritch Ichor found in your maps influenced by the Eater of Worlds have a chance to be duplicated. Eater-influenced monster packs have a rare chance to contain an additional Touching Tentacle Mass. The Touching Tentacle Mass is a floating ball of tentacles that chases the character, exploding shortly after it reaches their location. This inflicts Livewire for a short duration, a potentially beneficial debuff that increases action speed , with the downside of dealing lightning damage over time. The Touching Tentacle Mass is invulnerable and drops no items.

Resolute Technique | Description | Resolute Technique (often referred to as RT ) is a keystone passive skill that will raise your chance to hit to 100%, ignoring all accuracy and evasion stats of the attacker and defender respectively, at the cost of preventing you from dealing critical strikes.
Resolute Technique | Mechanics | Because elemental damage will no longer critically strike, most elemental status ailments will not apply unless another source adds chance. Skills such as Glacial Hammer and Burning Arrow have a built-in chance to inflict elemental status ailments, and for example, targets cursed with Conductivity have a chance to be shocked when hit with any lightning damage.
Resolute Technique | Mechanics | Sources of guaranteed critical strikes, such as Trypanon and the Diamond Shrine , have no effect on a character with the Resolute Technique.
Resolute Technique | Mechanics | Spells inherently can't be evaded, so they don't benefit from Resolute Technique, but it still takes away their ability to crit.
Resolute Technique | Mechanics | Attack hits can still be blocked , even with Resolute Technique.
Resolute Technique | Location | Resolute Technique is located on the west edge of the tree, across the Disemboweling passive cluster.
Resource Reallocation | Description | Resource Reallocation is an atlas passive skill. It increases the chance of adding 2 tiers instead of 1 to that incursion room if killing the non-resident architect of that room (i.e. keep that room's architect which is always on the bottom, killing the non-resident architect which is always on the top. This does not apply to tier 0 room which the two architects are both non-resident.)
Resource Reallocation | Description | Note that atlas passive skill tree does not apply to Map from Kirac's atlas mission. It also does not apply to map that is not on atlas, with Vaal Temple Map and Shaper Guardian Maps are exception.

Righteous Path | Description | Righteous Path is a notable passive skill only found on a Small Cluster Jewel that have the enchantment Added Small Passive Skills grant: 6% increased Mana Reservation Efficiency of Skills or a Megalomaniac which has 3 random notables.
Righteous Path | Calculations | Zealotry has 50% increased Mana Reservation Efficiency reduces Zealotry aura reservation to:
Righteous Path | Calculations | 50 % × 100 % 100 % + 50 % = 33.33 % \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\dfrac {50\%\times 100\%}{100\%+50\%}}=33.33\%
Righteous Path | Calculations | Since notable passive skills from cluster jewels are stackable, if the player does not have other increased/reduce (Mana) Reservation Efficiency mod (i.e. does not take into account of Added Small Passive Skills grant: 6% increased Mana Reservation Efficiency of Skills ), other than two Righteous Path, then the mana reservation reduced to:
Righteous Path | Calculations | 50 % × 100 % 100 % + ( 50 % + 50 % ) = 25.00 % \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\dfrac {50\%\times 100\%}{100\%+(50\%+50\%)}}=25.00\%
Righteous Path | Calculations | Note that there is a diminishing marginal return so that the mana reservation never equal to zero even stacking Reservation Efficiency towards positive infinity.
Righteous Path | Mods | It was able to spawn in Medium or Large Cluster Jewel with the following enchantments : Added Small Passive Skills grant: 3% increased effect of Non-Curse Auras from your Skills , or or Added [.] grant: 10% increased Elemental Damage or Added [.] grant: 12% increased Cold Damage or Added [.] grant: 12% increased Fire Damage or Added [.] grant: 12% increased Lightning Damage. Except the aura enchantment on Medium Cluster Jewel, the mod is spawn disabled on those enchantments since version 3.16.0.

Seasoned Swordplay | Description | Seasoned Swordplay is a notable passive skill.
Seasoned Swordplay | Mechanic | The formula of Reservation Efficiency is Resource Reserved = Base Reserve % 100 % + Total Reserve Efficiency % \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\text{Resource Reserved}}={\dfrac {{\text{Base Reserve }}\%}{100\%+{\text{Total Reserve Efficiency }}\%}}
Seasoned Swordplay | Mechanic | So that for the currently two stance skill gems : Blood and Sand and Flesh and Stone , they reserved 6.67% (from 10%) and 16.67% (from 25%) mana respectively with this passive skill allocated. The efficiency value is addictive (e.g. from one of the Attack Masteries ) , so that it has diminishing marginal return to make the mana (life) reservation never go to zero. Note that unless allocated via anointment , there is an un-skipable small passive skill Stance Reservation Efficiency before the notable. So that for this cluster alone, the reservation efficiency will be increased by 60% so that the reservation would be 6.25% and 15.63% respectively.
Seasoned Swordplay | Location | Southwest of the Duelist 's starting location. The un-skippable small passive skill of this cluster is Stance Reservation Efficiency. And then player has a choice to allocate either Attack Damage in Blood Stance or Attack Speed in Sand Stance to connect to the Seasoned Swordplay notable.

Second Sight | Description | Second Sight is a keystone passive skill which causes the character to be permanently blinded. It grants more melee critical strike chance while the character is blinded. Additionally, being blinded will not reduce the character's light radius.

Secrets of Suffering | Description | Secrets of Suffering is an item exclusive keystone passive skill. Upon taking it, the character will be unable to directly Ignite , Chill , Freeze or Shock enemies, but will inflict Scorch , Brittle , and Sapped upon a critical strike.
Secrets of Suffering | Description | However, the magnitude of the alternative ailments still requires the matching elemental damage. Otherwise, a zero magnitude ailment will be discarded by the game server.
Secrets of Suffering | Mechanics | Chill and Shock can still be applied indirectly with;
Secrets of Suffering | Mechanics | Notably, Chilled Ground from Creeping Frost does NOT work despite being worded similarly to all the working sources above. Hydrosphere & Wintertide Brand do not work either, but they are more intuitive as the source of Chill is more obviously the player.
Secrets of Suffering | Mechanics | Ignite can still be applied indrectly with;
Secrets of Suffering | Mechanics | Hexblast 's Chaos Damage can inflict ailments modifier does not work with Secrets of Suffering. Hexblast only allows Chill, Ignite & Shock to be applied, and Secrets of Suffering will disable Hexblast from applying them, without allowing Hexblast to apply Scorch/Brittle/Sap at more than 0% magnitude (unless the spell also deals Fire/Cold/Lightning damage respectively).

Shaping the Mountains | Description | Maps Dropped in Areas have #% chance to be 1 tier higher : This stat stacks additively with similar stats from the Atlas Passive Tree and Voidstones ; if the chance exceeds 100%, the excess chance instead applies to chance to be 2 tiers higher, and so on. [1]

Speaker of the Dead | Description | Speaker of the Dead is an Atlas passive skill and Atlas keystone , specifically for Tormented spirits encounters.
Speaker of the Dead | Mechanics | Speaker of the Dead causes Tormented Spirits to be unable to possess monsters, but instead are able to Possess players for 20 seconds in maps. Players possessed by Tormented Spirits can apply a Tormented Spirit's Touch modifier to up to 40 nearby normal or magic monsters per Tormented Spirit possessing the player. This number is counted individually for each different Tormented Spirit.
Speaker of the Dead | Mechanics | Tormented Spirits in your Maps can Possess Players for 20 seconds : Making contact with a Tormented Spirit grants a buff, providing 35% increased Damage, 35% increased Attack Speed, 35% increased Cast Speed, and 35% increased Movement Speed. This buff stacks based on the number of Tormented Spirits possessing you. This buff does stack with the similar buff from Fairgraves' Tricorne.
Speaker of the Dead | Mechanics | Additionally, being possessed by a Tormented Spirit grants the corresponding " X's Grip " buff listed below; note that certain stats may not be directly reflected on the character's stats or tooltip (e.g. Attacks cause Bleeding). A player can have multiple different Grip buffs at once; a duplicate Tormented Spirit cannot possess a player that already has the corresponding Grip buff.
Speaker of the Dead | Tormented Spirit modifiers | Note: information is based on inferences from metadata and may not be 100% accurate.
Speaker of the Dead | Unusual | These Tormented Spirits can only appear in maps affected by a Torment Scarab of Peculiarity. Every monster Possessed by an usual variant will drop an item specific to the tormented spirit. (map, scarab or unique item) The Betrayer and Heretic Touched monsters also have a chance to drop a specific item (scarab or map depending on the spirit). The chance is supposedly 10%, following the metadata which may not be accurate. The scarabs dropped this way doesn't seem to be affected by modifiers on the atlas tree, as notable nodes such as Loved by the Sun doesn't prevent abyss scarabs to drop.
Speaker of the Dead | Location | As of version 3.22.0, it is located near the center-left of the Atlas passive skill tree connected to the Torment cluster containing Unrelenting Torment.

Spiteful Presence | Calculations | Hatred has 50% increased Mana Reservation Efficiency reduces Hatred aura reservation to:
Spiteful Presence | Calculations | 50 % × 100 % 100 % + 50 % = 33.33 % \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\dfrac {50\%\times 100\%}{100\%+50\%}}=33.33\%
Spiteful Presence | Calculations | Since notable passive skills from cluster jewels are stackable, if the player does not have other increased/reduce (Mana) Reservation Efficiency mod (i.e. does not take into account of Added Small Passive Skills grant: 6% increased Mana Reservation Efficiency of Skills , the enchantment of the magic/rare Small Cluster Jewel that this passive currently able to obtain from), other than two Spiteful Presence, then the mana reservation reduced to:
Spiteful Presence | Calculations | 50 % × 100 % 100 % + ( 50 % + 50 % ) = 25.00 % \color [rgb]{0.6392156862745098,0.5529411764705883,0.42745098039215684}{\dfrac {50\%\times 100\%}{100\%+(50\%+50\%)}}=25.00\%
Spiteful Presence | Calculations | Note that there is a diminishing marginal return so that the mana reservation never equal to zero even stacking Reservation Efficiency towards positive infinity.
Spiteful Presence | Mods | It can also appears on a legacy Medium Cluster Jewel with the enchantment : Added Small Passive Skills grant: 3% increased effect of Non-Curse Auras from your Skills

Tempered by War | Description | For more information about taking damage as another element, see Damage taken as.
Tempered by War | Mechanics | When combined with a "taken as Fire" Avian Twins Talisman no cold or lightning damage from hits is taken for the chosen element.
Tempered by War | Mechanics | When combined with Mahuxotl's Machination no cold or lightning damage is taken; it is taken as either Fire or Chaos damage.
Tempered by War | Mechanics | When combined with Sublime Vision (Purity of Fire variation) and a Dawnbreaker or a Watcher's Eye with (10-20)% of Cold and Lightning Damage taken as Fire Damage while affected by Purity of Fire PurityOfFireColdAndLightningTakenAsFire Intrinsic (10-20)% of Cold and Lightning Damage taken as Fire Damage while affected by Purity of Fire mod with max rolls, no cold and lightning damage is taken; it is taken entirely as Fire Damage. This can also be combined with Chaos Inoculation to negate the need for cold, lightning, and chaos resistances.
Tempered by War | Mechanics | In cases where all damage is taken as another element (not just the hit damage), it is safe to not gear for the original resistance at all. Taking damage as another element also prevents element-specific penetration (e.g. The Shaper 's cold penetration) from applying.
Tempered by War | Mechanics | Note that due to the way less modifiers work with negative values, if cold or lightning resistance are negative, Tempered by War will actually raise those resistances (though never above -1%). This can be a problem for a Doryani's Prototype build.

That didn't happen! | Description | That didn't happen! is a notable Bloodline Ascendancy passive skill from the Delirious Bloodline that grants less damage taken from hits , but causes a portion of damage taken to be dealt as life loss after 4 seconds. In addition, any non- cluster non- passage jewels socketed into your passive skill tree are disabled.
That didn't happen! | Mechanics | Four seconds after each Hit you take, lose Life equal to 40% of Damage taken from that Hit : This stat causes a portion of damage taken from hits to be taken again as a delayed life loss effect. The life loss effect is calculated after accounting for damage mitigation from the original hit. Note that life loss is not considered taking a hit or taking damage, and cannot be further modified or mitigated. In a vacuum, factoring in the 40% less Damage taken stat provided by this passive, this passive provides an effective 16% less damage taken from hits. The life loss from this effect can kill the character. This effect differs from Petrified Blood in that the delayed life loss from each hit happens all at once after 4 seconds, as opposed to over a 4 second time frame, so life recoup cannot directly negate the life loss.
That didn't happen! | Mechanics | Non-Cluster, Non-Passage Jewels Socketed in your Passive Skill Tree have no effect : All jewels socketed in the passive tree that are not cluster jewels or passage jewels ( unique jewels that allow allocation of unconnected passive skills) have their stats disabled. It does not affect jewels socketed anywhere else (i.e. Abyss jewels socketed in equipment with Abyssal sockets ).
That didn't happen! | Mechanics | The following passage jewels are unaffected:
That didn't happen! | Mechanics | Taking this passive skill also causes random Insanity effects to occur, which are harmless but ominous chat messages or animations.

The Agnostic | Description | The Agnostic is a keystone passive skill that removes your energy shield and drains mana per second to recover your life while you are not at full life.
The Agnostic | Description | This skill node is essential for the Mana before Life defensive technique, provided you have enough Mana recovery to maintain it.
The Agnostic | Mechanics | "Full Life" is used in the literal sense, rather than the "no Life left to recover" sense used by flasks. If you have any Life reserved, you will sacrifice Mana continuously even if your unreserved Life is full. Forcing the full life condition (i.e. Coward's Chains ) does not change this behavior, but the You count as on Full Life while at 90% of maximum Life or above Life Mastery will change the life threshold for when The Agnostic activates.
The Agnostic | Mechanics | While at full life and taking damage over time, the mana sacrificed will be equal to the total life lost per second, up to the maximum of 20% of your mana [1].
The Agnostic | Mechanics | Life Recovery Rate will affect the recovery of the Agnostic Keystone, but it will not affect the loss of mana at all [2].
The Agnostic | Location | The Agnostic is located on the far left side of the skill tree, to the west of the Templar's starting point.
The Agnostic | Location | This keystone can also be obtained from the tree by using a legacy Militant Faith jewel with modifier Carved to glorify (2000-10000) new faithful converted by High Templar Venarius.
